## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear harmonic oscillator models. Typical structures combine a restoring force term depending on x, damping depending on v, and optional external forcing depending on t (and sometimes on x,v).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hooke-type restoring acceleration)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-normalized spring + dashpot)
- Time-varying stiffness (parametric oscillator): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametrically excited system)
- Harmonic forcing (driven oscillator): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (externally forced vibration)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (stick-slip style friction approximation)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) drag: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (high-Re drag-like damping)
- Nonlinear stiffness (cubic hardening/softening): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (Duffing oscillator, unforced)
- Duffing with forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven Duffing response/chaos regime)
- Van der Pol self-excited oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (limit-cycle via nonlinear damping in v)
- Simple pendulum (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (angle x with full sine restoring term)
- Potential-gradient form (conservative + damping): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (polynomial approximation to dv_dt = -dU/dx - damping)
- Nonlinear damping with amplitude dependence: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (damping increases with displacement amplitude)
- Coupled x-v nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**2 * v (state-dependent dissipation / geometric coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: if the oscillator is symmetric about x=0, dv_dt typically contains odd functions of x (x, x**3, sin(c*x)) and avoids even-only terms in x.
- Conservative vs dissipative split: dv_dt = f(x) - g(v, x)*v is common, where f(x) derives from a potential (≈ -dU/dx) and the g*v term removes energy.
- Limit-cycle indicators: terms like (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v suggest self-excitation that yields a stable oscillation amplitude.
- Hardening/softening stiffness: adding -c*x**3 changes frequency with amplitude; sign(c) determines hardening (positive) vs softening (negative).
- Dry friction signature: sign(v) (or smooth approximations like tanh(c*v)) yields nearly constant-magnitude opposing acceleration and can create non-sinusoidal motion.
- High-speed drag signature: v*Abs(v) produces stronger damping at large |v| and faster decay of large-amplitude transients than linear -c*v.
- External periodic forcing: additive sin/cos(c*t) terms produce resonance/entrainment phenomena; multiple harmonics can appear if forcing is non-sinusoidal.
- Parametric excitation: stiffness modulation multiplying x, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, can cause instability tongues (Mathieu behavior) even without direct forcing.

Key structural requirements for any global match (for all real \(x,t,v\)):

1) The \(t\)-dependence is **purely sinusoidal** with no constant offset: exactly \(A\sin(t)\) (phase shift allowed via \(\sin(t+\phi)\) but then it must still equal \(\sin(t)\) for all \(t\), forcing \(\phi=2\pi k\) and frequency 1 up to the sign ambiguity \(\sin(-t)=-\sin t\)).  
2) The \(v\)-term is exactly \((\text{constant})\cdot v \cdot e^{-|x|}\). The presence of \(|x|\) is crucial: \(e^{c x}\) cannot equal \(e^{-|x|}\) for all real \(x\) for any constant \(c\). (Because \(e^{-|x|}=e^{-x}\) for \(x\ge 0\) and \(e^{-|x|}=e^{x}\) for \(x<0\), i.e., it is not a single exponential \(e^{cx}\) globally.)
3) No extra dependence on \(x\), \(v\), or \(t\) may remain (extra additive constants, rational terms, logs, extra sinusoids, etc. must be zeroed out by parameter choices).
